<p>UNIT THREE: SANITATION</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This third unit will enable you understand the importance of excreta disposal, refuse disposal, water and waste disposal, environmental management, types of housing and indoor air pollution, hand washing procedure, vector borne diseases, their transmission and control of vectors and pests, community led total sanitation, school led total sanitation which all contribute to the health status of a community.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unit-objectives">Unit Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this Unit you should</p>
<ol>
<li>Describe excreta disposal methods</li>
<li>explain the importance and steps in community sanitation (CLTS)</li>
<li>identify the main types of waste and the refuse disposal methods,</li>
<li>explain vector borne diseases, their transmission and control of vectors and pests</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="topic-one">Topic One<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#topic-one" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Topic name</th><th>Introduction to the Principles and Concepts of Waste Management</th></tr></thead></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definition">Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Waste management refers to the many methods and processes of dealing with waste at every stage from generation and collection through to final disposal.</p>
<p>â˜‘ Waste can be categorized as liquid waste or solid waste depending on its physical state.
â˜‘ It can also be categorized as hazardous or non-hazardous</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hazardous-and-non-hazardous-waste-hazardous-wastes">Hazardous and non-hazardous waste Hazardous wastes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hazardous-and-non-hazardous-waste-hazardous-wastes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Hazardous wastes are defined as wastes that have one or more of the following properties.</p>
<p>â˜‘ Corrosive (substances that cause damage on contact, e.g. acids).
â˜‘ Ignitable (materials that can catch fire easily like benzene).
â˜‘ Toxic (materials that can be poisonous to humans when inhaled or ingested, or come in contact with skin or mucous membranes).
â˜‘ Reactive (substances that can yield a harmful chemical if they react with other substances).</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> infectious (substances that are capable of causing or communicating infection) Non-hazardous wastes include all other types of waste.</p>
<ul>
<li>Biodegradable and non-biodegradable wastes
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> Biodegradable wastes are those that can be broken down (decomposed) into their constituent elements by bacteria and other microorganisms. example Human and animal wastes, food waste, paper, and agricultural wastes.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="liquid-waste">Liquid waste<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#liquid-waste" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> It includes human waste, runoff (storm water or flood water), sullage, industrial wastewater and other forms of wastewater from different sources.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> Human waste is mainly composed of faeces and urine, which together are known as excreta. All human body waste is classed as liquid waste.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> The mixture of human waste with wastewater is known as sewage and also sometimes known as blackwater.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> Runoff is simply rainwater that collects on the ground and runs off into channels, ditches and rivers.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> Sullage, also known as greywater, is water that has been used for washing in bathrooms and kitchens; it does not include human waste
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> The decomposing bacteria found in pit latrines and septic tanks do not require oxygen and are called anaerobic bacteria.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> The digested waste matter is called sludge.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="liquid-waste-management">liquid waste Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#liquid-waste-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> basic requirements for a human waste (excreta) disposal method
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> Surface water must not be contaminated.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> There should be no contamination of groundwater that may, in turn, contaminate springs or wells.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> Excreta should not be accessible to flies or other animals.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> There should be no handling of excreta; where this is unavoidable, it should be kept to a minimum.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> There should be no odours or unsightly conditions.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> The method used should be simple and inexpensive in construction and operation.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> The method should last for at least five years to be cost-effective.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="factors-to-consider-when-selecting-liquid-waste-disposal-facilities">factors to consider when selecting liquid waste disposal facilities<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-to-consider-when-selecting-liquid-waste-disposal-facilities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> Topography and geological formations
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> Abundance or scarcity of water:
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> Cultural acceptability
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> Affordability
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> Safety to users
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> Accessibility
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> Availability of resources and infrastructure
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> The presence of human skills
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âœ“</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âœ“</span></span></span></span></span> Energy source and pit emptying requirements</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Solid wastes
âœ“ Solid waste is defined as any waste that is dry in form and is discarded by people as unwanted.</p>
<p>Classifications of solid waste
Solid waste can be classified into two categories by its characteristics. These are:
âž¤ Organic solid waste
âž¤ Inorganic Solid waste
Organic solid waste:
âž¤ Wastes that are generally biodegradable and decompose in the process of which emits offensive and irritating smell when left unattended.
Inorganic solid waste:
âž¤ Solid matter that does not decompose at any rate
This category of waste matter may be combustible depending on the type of the nature of the material they constitute
Classes of solid waste</p>
<ol>
<li>Domestic wastes e.g. Food wastes, Paper, cardboard, plastics, textiles, leather, yard wastes, wood, glass, metals, ashes, special wastes (e.g. Bulky items, consumer electronics, white goods, batteries, oil tires),</li>
<li>Industrial wastes- Wastes from the manufacturing sector, example Housekeeping wastes, packaging, food wastes, hazardous wastes, ashes, and special wastes.</li>
<li>Wastes from commercial Stores, hotels, restaurants, markets, office buildings, etc Paper, cardboard, plastics, wood, food wastes, glass, metals, special wastes, hazardous wastes</li>
<li>Institutional wastes- from Schools, hospitals, prisons, government centers</li>
<li>Construction and demolition. Example wastes from New construction sites, road repair, renovation sites, demolition of buildings Wood, Steel, concrete, dirt, etc.</li>
<li>Street wastes, wastes from the streets and all activities there. Example cigarette ends, wrappers, fruits peels and bus tickets</li>
<li>Industrial process wastes, scrap materials, off- specification products, slag tailings</li>
<li>Agriculture wastes from farms, gardens and ranches. Includes tree branches</li>
<li>Special wastes- from hospitals etc. example human tissues, amputated organs, bandages, reagents, expired drugs etc
Health implications of solid wastes
â—‹ Diseases
â—‹ Vectors
â—‹ Injuries
Environmental implications of solid waste</li>
</ol>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Pollution of air, water and grounds</li>
<li>Clogging of drains</li>
<li>Fire links</li>
<li>Occupy useful space</li>
<li>Economic implications</li>
<li>Recycling could result in creation of new products</li>
<li>Recycling could create employment</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="why-we-need-manage-solid-wastes">Why we need manage solid wastes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#why-we-need-manage-solid-wastes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Prevent and control diseases.</li>
<li>Eliminate nuisance</li>
<li>Prevent mechanical injury for example from broken bottles, syringes and tins</li>
<li>Prevent fires</li>
<li>Prevent pollution</li>
<li>Avoid wastage of resources</li>
<li>Creation of space</li>
<li>Prevent blockage of drains,</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="elements-of-solid-waste-management-system">Elements of solid waste management system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#elements-of-solid-waste-management-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Waste generation</li>
<li>On-site handling (sorting, storage and processing)</li>
<li>Collection</li>
<li>Transfer and transport</li>
<li>Processing and recovery</li>
<li>Disposal</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="risks-and-problems-associated-with-solid-wastes">Risks and Problems Associated with Solid wastes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risks-and-problems-associated-with-solid-wastes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It can be best media for the growth of microorganisms</li>
<li>Attraction of arthropods such as common housefly, mosquito, etc</li>
<li>Attraction of rodents and other animals e.g. rats mice dogs cats</li>
<li>Open dump can contaminate water sources</li>
<li>Can contaminate food supply and cause food borne disease</li>
<li>Hospital and pathological wastes are potential disease carrying waste products</li>
<li>It can create fire accident</li>
<li>It can create nuisance: Bad odor, smoke, dust Aesthetical problem</li>
<li>Discomfort: sneezing, coughing</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solid-waste-management">Solid waste management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solid-waste-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Refers to the discipline associated with the control of generation, storage, collection, transfer and transport, processing, and disposal of solid wastes in a manner that is in accordance with the best principles of public health, economics, engineering, conservations, and that is also responsive to public attitudes.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Classification of stages of solid waste management/functional elements of solid waste management.</p>
<ul>
<li>onsite handling</li>
<li>storage and processing</li>
<li>Collection. transfer and transport</li>
<li>resource recovery and processing</li>
<li>Disposal.</li>
</ul>
<p>Integrated solid waste management (ISWM).
âœ“ ISWM means considering not only the appropriate disposal of solid waste but integrating this with other management options such as minimising waste production, recycling, composting and other waste recovery options.
âœ“ The advantages of ISWM are that it considers all options and aims to manage waste in ways that are most effective in protecting human health and the environment.
âœ“ ISWM can also have many economic and social benefits for your community</p>
<p>Solid waste disposal methods
â—‹ The major aim of refuse disposal is to change the physical characteristics of refuse and render it free from odor, less attractive to vectors and diseases.</p>
<p>methods of solid waste disposal</p>
<ol>
<li>crude dumping</li>
<li>Hog feeding</li>
<li>Incineration</li>
<li>Sanitary landfill/controlled tipping</li>
<li>Composting</li>
<li>Dumping into water bodies</li>
</ol>

<p>International categorization of medical wastes</p>
<ol>
<li>Low risk waste
Communal waste
Solid waste which does not contain high risk wastes, example bottles, office paper, boxes and packaging materials</li>
<li>Highly infectious wastes</li>
</ol>
<p>24</p>
<p>25</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Infectious waste
&gt; Example blood and blood products, body fluids, items contaminated by blood, serum, plasma, cultures, bandages and surgical dressings.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Anatomical wastes
&gt; Human tissues, body parts, fetuses, placenta, organs and tissues infected with human pathogens.</p>

&gt; Needles and syringes, scalpel blades, suture needles, razors, infusion sets contaminated broken glass.</p>

&gt; Expired medications, discarded live vaccines</p>

&gt; radiating residues produced as a result of radio therapy and diagnosis</p>

<p>wastes with high content of heavy metals
&gt; Example batteries, broken thermometers</p>
</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="topic">Topic<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#topic" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Topic name</th><th>Healthful housing</th></tr></thead></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Every family and individual has a basic right to a decent home and a suitable living environment.</li>
<li>Housing is a basic prerequisite for health. This right is noted in the constitutions of many countries, including Kenya.</li>
<li>However, a significant proportion of the population in rural and urban areas in most parts of the world does not possess suitable healthful housing.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="housing">Housing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#housing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>is the physical structure that man uses for shelter and the environs of that structure including all necessary services, facilities, equipment, and devices needed or desired for the physical, mental, and social wellbeing of the family and individual.</p>
<ul>
<li>The goal of housing is preserving oneâ€™s health. This is the purpose of a physical building and its immediate environment.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Standard Housing:</strong>- is a house that is properly planned and constructed, comfortable, safe to live in and fulfill the basic housing necessities ( constructed in proper site, provided with safe and adequate water supply, safe and proper waste disposal , adequate light, space, well ventilated, etc.</p>
<p><strong>Substandard Housing:</strong>- is a house, which is poorly sited, planned and constructed, inadequate floor space for the family (overcrowded), poorly maintained and does not in general comply</p>
<p>with the more important sanitary facilities.</p>
<p><strong>Slum:</strong>- is an area in which substandard housing predominates and frequently accompanied with overcrowding.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="conditions-directly-or-indirectly-responsible-for-the-occurrence-of-substandard-housing">conditions directly or indirectly responsible for the occurrence of substandard housing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#conditions-directly-or-indirectly-responsible-for-the-occurrence-of-substandard-housing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>â˜‘ With the movement of people to cities, urban areas are congested, and desirable housing become unattainable.</li>
<li>â˜‘ Inadequate transportation facilities to and from work placemakes it necessary for any people to accept less desirable</li>
<li>â˜‘ Housing, in the cities, closer to their work places.</li>
<li>â˜‘ Low income to afford satisfactory housing.</li>
<li>â˜‘ Lack of housing legislation to enforce suitable zoning, building, and sanitation and poor support from courts.</li>
<li>â˜‘ Mismatch of the rate of construction of housing and rehabilitation to keep pace with population growth.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-of-housing">principles of housing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-housing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>â˜ Protection against communicable diseases;</li>
<li>â˜ Protection against injuries,</li>
<li>â˜ Prevention of poisonings and chronic diseases;</li>
<li>â˜ Reducing psychological and social stresses to a minimum;</li>
<li>â˜ Improving the housing environment;</li>
<li>â˜ Making informed use of housing;</li>
<li>â˜ Protecting population at special risk.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="basic-requirements-of-healthful-housing">Basic requirements of healthful housing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#basic-requirements-of-healthful-housing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>satisfaction of physiological needs</li>
<li>protection against psychological and social stresses</li>
<li>protection against infection</li>
<li>protection against accidents</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-satisfaction-of-fundamental-physiological-needs">1. Satisfaction of Fundamental Physiological needs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-satisfaction-of-fundamental-physiological-needs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>â˜‘ Any housing meant for human habitation should avoid all factors that may affect the normal physiological activities of the body of occupants.</li>
<li>â˜‘ The conditions listed below have direct or indirect associations with physiological and metabolic activities of the human body.</li>
</ul>
<p>i. The house should maintain thermal environment that will avoid undue heat loss from the human body during cold weather conditions.
ii. It should also maintain the thermal environment that will permit adequate heat loss from the human body in warm weather conditions.
iii. It has to be constructed in such a way that it can be well ventilated, or provided with artificial ventilation facilities
iv. 2. Provision of adequate day light (sunlight) illumination and avoidance of undue day light glare such as unnecessary reflection in the room. Adequate sunlight helps the body to generate vitamin â€˜Dâ€™ and also it has a bactericidal effect.
v. Provision of atmosphere of reasonable chemical and bacteriological purity i.e. indoor atmosphere should be free of chemical substances, dust particles, smoke,</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>microorganisms and particulate matters.</p>
<p>vi. Protection against excessive outdoor and indoor noise.</p>
<p>vii. Provision of adequate artificial light preferably electricity to avoid possible indoor air pollution.</p>
<p>viii. Provision of adequate space for exercise, gardening and for the play of children</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-satisfaction-of-fundamental-psychological-needs">2. Satisfaction of Fundamental Psychological Needs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-satisfaction-of-fundamental-psychological-needs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Each Family member requires some sort of privacy for specific personal affairs. separate bedrooms for the sexes are required at the minimum ages of 10 years and sleeping rooms of children over two years of age, should be separate from parents, for various reasons.</li>
<li>The house should also secure the family members from the frightening conditions such as robbers, wild animals, reptiles, scorpions, etc.</li>
<li>Provision of facilities which make possible the performance of the tasks of the household without undue physical and mental fatigue, and possibilities for aesthetic satisfaction in the home and its surroundings play a vital role in promotion of psychological wellbeing of the family members.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-protection-against-communicable-diseases">3. Protection against Communicable Diseases<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-protection-against-communicable-diseases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A good house must satisfy the need for protection of occupants from risk of communicable diseases through provision of safe water supply, proper excreta and refuse disposal, prevention of vermin, insects, rodents, and proper storage for foods.</li>
<li>Provision of adequate sleeping spaces minimizes the spread of contagious infections such as scabies, and other dermatological problems, pediculosis, etc.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-protection-against-accidental-injuries">4. Protection against accidental Injuries<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-protection-against-accidental-injuries" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The incidence of indoor accidents is directly related to the housing condition, its engineering design and arrangements of physical objects in the house such as the different household equipment, and work methods etc.</p>
<p>Improving housing and maintaining it, somehow can significantly reduce the rate of such accidents.</p>
<ol>
<li>Erection of dwelling with such materials and methods of construction as to minimize danger of accidents due to collapse of any part of the construction. Termite infestation sometimes causes accidents by weakening joints or stairways.</li>
<li>Control of conditions likely to cause fire or promote its spread. This calls for construction methods and materials, which do not result in fire hazards</li>
<li>Provision of adequate emergency facilities for escape in case of fire, fire extinguishing facilities like fire hydrant, chemical extinguishers or locally available materials like sand and soil should be available at close proximity to the house.</li>
<li>Protection against danger of electric shocks in which proper electrical wiring is essential, such as proper installation of sockets, insulation of electric wires using conduits.</li>
<li>Protection against gas poisoning, which calls for proper ventilation or venting of the room to dilute the indoor air.</li>
<li>Protection against falls and other mechanical injuries in the house.</li>
<li>Protection of the neighborhood against the hazards of automobile traffic i.e. location of housing projects should be considered with traffic conditions in mind.</li>
</ol>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>29</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="facilities-required-for-healthful-housing">Facilities Required for Healthful Housing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#facilities-required-for-healthful-housing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-ventilation">1. Ventilation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-ventilation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ventilation is the process of supplying air to or removing it from any enclosed space by natural or mechanical means.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="methods-of-ventilating-a-house">Methods of Ventilating a House<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-of-ventilating-a-house" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are two means of ventilation: -</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Natural ventilation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Artificial ventilation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Natural ventilation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It involves the use of natural forces of air diffusion and current by having properly built doors, windows, (such as fanlight, hopper or sliding sash windows).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Natural ventilation is an efficient, cheap and satisfactory form of effecting air movement in the house.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The disadvantages of natural ventilation are:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It is dependent upon wind direction - It does not control the possibility of entrance of smoky, dusty, and generally undesirable air.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Artificial (mechanical) Ventilation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It involves the use of mechanical apparatus such as fans and air conditioners. Such mechanical ventilators set air current in motion.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-lighting">2. Lighting<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-lighting" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>There are two types (sources) of lighting:</li>
<li>Natural lighting e.g. sunlight</li>
<li>Artificial lighting - These are the systems of a man made lighting</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="characteristics-of-good-lighting">Characteristics of good lighting<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-good-lighting" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Good lighting systems are those that fulfill the following characteristics:</li>
<li>a. Must be adequate in power</li>
<li>b. Constant and uniform</li>
<li>c. Flickers and vibrations are absent</li>
<li>d. Absence of glare and shadows.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="3-heating-of-a-house">3. Heating of a House<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-heating-of-a-house" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Heating system of a building is necessary to maintain body temperature specially in cold regions.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-space-and-occupancy">4. Space and Occupancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-space-and-occupancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>There is a direct relationship between good housing and good mental health, since suitable housing is a prerequisite for a mental wellbeing.</li>
<li>The house needs to satisfy the following requirements in order to promote the psychological wellbeing of the inhabitants:-</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>a) Provision of adequate privacy for family members: Privacy is the ability of a person(s) to carryout an activity commenced without interruption or interference either by sight or sound. It deals with a â€œroom of oneâ€™s ownâ€. Overcrowding condition is the main cause of lack of privacy.</p>
<p>The maximum number of persons who may occupy any dwelling house is dependent upon three main factors:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Separation of the sexes.</li>
<li>The number of rooms available.</li>
<li>The floor area of the rooms to be occupied.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="effects-of-occupancy">Effects of occupancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-of-occupancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are five effects of human occupancy in unventilated rooms. These are:</p>
<ol>
<li>Decrease in oxygen content</li>
<li>Increase the amount of carbon dioxide</li>
<li>Increase in organic matter (odor, bacteria from mouth, skin, clothing, etc)</li>
<li>Increase the temperature and humidity of the room.</li>
<li>Increase the transmission of communicable diseases such as skin disease, TB, etc.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-housing-sanitation">5. Housing Sanitation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-housing-sanitation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A good house is that which prompts health and enjoyable living.</p>
<p>It has the following characteristics:-</p>
<p>a. That which is sited in a well-drained areas with good construction
b. That which provides separate accommodations for human and animals
c. That which is free from dampness and wetness
d. Have adequate natural and artificial light and ventilation
e. Should have a separate kitchen and store
f. Should be rodent proof
g. Should have clean and cleanable latrine
h. Should have proper sewerage system (in case of water carriage waste disposal system)
i. Should have an appropriate way of removing refuse (proper solid waste management)
j. Must have safe and adequate supply of water within or nearby.
k. Has adequate space for recreation, play of children, and for physical exercise</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indoor-air-pollution">Indoor Air Pollution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indoor-air-pollution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Air is absolutely essential for sustainability of life.</li>
<li>The composition of pure ambient air</li>
</ul>
<p>Nitrogen--- 78.1%</p>
<p>Oxygen---20.9%</p>
<p>Carbon dioxide---0.03%</p>
<p>Argon gas, Neon, Helium, Hydrogen, Krypton, are also present in the air with a very small proportion in the atmosphere.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sources-of-indoor-air-pollution">Sources of indoor air pollution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources-of-indoor-air-pollution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Indoor air pollutants are generally grouped into the following major sources:</p>
<ol>
<li>Radon gas â€“ it seeps into homes from the soil, brick, concrete and stone.</li>
<li>Combustion products</li>
<li>Building materials and chemicals e.g foam insulation floor covering (carpet) and textile products, furniture polish, disinfectants, solvents, paint, etc</li>
</ol>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Biological aerosols and house hold dusts example Microbes are emitted during coughing, laughing, speaking and sneezing</li>
<li>Decomposition processes</li>
<li>Respiration</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="health-effects-of-indoor-air-pollution-upon-occupants">Health Effects of Indoor Air Pollution upon Occupants:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#health-effects-of-indoor-air-pollution-upon-occupants" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="nitrogen-dioxide-no2">Nitrogen Dioxide (NO2)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nitrogen-dioxide-no2" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Cause respiratory tract irritation and inflammation.</li>
<li>Cause an increased air-flow resistance in respiratory tract.</li>
<li>Cause an increased risk of the respiratory infection.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="carbon-monoxide-co">Carbon Monoxide (CO)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#carbon-monoxide-co" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>&gt; Carbon monoxide combines readily with blood hemoglobin to form carboxyl hemoglobin, thereby reducing the amount of hemoglobin available to carry oxygen to other parts of the body.
&gt; Hemoglobin has a greater affinity to carbon monoxide than for oxygen.
&gt; Excessive exposure results in reduced oxygen available to heart, brain, and muscles leading to weakness, head ache, dizziness, nausea, vomiting, an impairment of psychomotor facilities, dimness of vision, coronary effects and then to death.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="sulfur-dioxide-so2">Sulfur Dioxide (SO2)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sulfur-dioxide-so2" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Broncho-constriction, often associated with wheezing and respiratory distress.</li>
<li>Impairment of lung function</li>
<li>Increased asthmatic attack.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="formaldehyde">Formaldehyde<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#formaldehyde" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>irritation of eyes and respiratory tract</li>
<li>Causes bronchial asthma at higher doses.</li>
<li>Cause occupational allergic contact dermatitis and skin irritation.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="tobacco-smoke">Tobacco smoke<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tobacco-smoke" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Eye, nose, and throat irritation</li>
<li>Nasal congestion and rhinorrhea.</li>
<li>Inflammation of the lower respiratory tract</li>
<li>Lung cancer</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="fungi-and-bacteria">Fungi and Bacteria<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fungi-and-bacteria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Hypersensitivity pneumonitis, causing cough, dyspnea, and fatigue and allergic rhinitis.</li>
<li>Humidifier fever, causing flu-like illness with fever, chills, myalgia, and malaise.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-of-indoor-air-pollution">Prevention of Indoor air pollution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-of-indoor-air-pollution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="generally-the-control-measures-for-indoor-air-pollution-are">Generally the control measures for indoor air pollution are:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#generally-the-control-measures-for-indoor-air-pollution-are" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Stove design improvement (to increase the efficiency of complete combustion)</li>
<li>Use separate kitchen as much as possible</li>
<li>Use of clean fuel</li>
<li>Improving house design and construction of proper ventilation</li>
<li>Health education on control measures of indoor air pollution.</li>
<li>Improving standard of living</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="topic-one">Topic One<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#topic-one" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Topic name</th><th>VECTORS AND RODENTS CONTROL</th></tr></thead></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definitions">Definitions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definitions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Rodents:- comprise a great number of mammals, ranging in size from the rats and mice to as large as the Porcupines and which belong to the order rodentia.</p>
<p>Vector(s):- refers arthropods or other invertebrates which transmit infection by inoculation into or through the skin or mucous membrane by biting or by deposit of infective materials on the skin or on food or other objects.</p>
<p>Biological vectors- are vectors that transmit disease pathogens after the multiplication or development of the pathogen in the insect gut or muscle. E.g. malarial mosquito</p>
<p>Insecticides: are substances or an agent that kill insects or other arthropods.</p>
<p>Insecticide formulation:- is the addition of substances ( solvent or diluents ) which enable a given chemical insecticide to be used to greatest advantage.</p>
<p>Mechanical vectors- are vectors that transmit pathogenic microorganisms without undertaking any developmental change. E.g. common house fly</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ways-of-vector-borne-disease-transmission">Ways of Vector Borne Disease Transmission:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ways-of-vector-borne-disease-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Mechanical disease transmission:- is a type of disease transmission in which the vector is no more than a carrier that transmit pathogens without any change either on the number or form of disease pathogens.</li>
<li>Biological disease transmission: In this type of disease transmission certain developmental pattern exists either in the vector or host or in both cases.</li>
<li>Transovarian (Hereditary) disease transmission:- is a type of disease transmission where by the causative agent is transmitted to the immature stage ( usually to egg ) from the adult insects / other arthropods who carry disease pathogens and when the infected egg complete its developmental stage, it become infective or can transmit the disease to man and other animals.</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-anopheles-mosquitoes">1. <p>BLACK FLY
Public Health Importance
â˜‘ Nuisance</p>
<p>Black flies can cause a very serious biting problem, since there bites can be painful.</p>
<p>Severity of the bites can cause localized swelling and inflammation frequently occurs, accompanied by intense irritation lasting for several days or even weeks.</p>
<p>â˜‘ Onchocerciasis / river blindness is the disease transmitted by the female black fly.</p>
<p>Repeated infection affects the eyes that lead to blindness</p>
<p>Vector control:
â˜‘ Insecticide spraying to control black flies has proved successful in certain areas.
â˜‘ Use of repellents such as diethyltoluamide
â˜‘ Bush clearing</p>
<p>Sand Fly
Public Health importance of phlebotamus sand fly
â˜‘ Nuisance, biting nuisance.
â˜‘ Leishmaniasis
â˜‘ Sandfly Fever/ 3 day fever</p>
<p>Control</p>
<ul>
<li>Controlled by residual sprays applied to walls, screens, fences, etc.</li>
<li>Personal protection can be achieved by applying efficient insect repellents</li>
<li>Mesh screens or nets with very small holes can afford some protection</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="house-fly">HOUSE FLY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#house-fly" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Breeding places Houseflies can breed practically in any moist, decaying or fermenting human, animal and plant wastes.</p>
<p>The following are some of the favourite breeding media:</p>
<ol>
<li>Human excreta: whenever exposed in open latrines, seepage pits, septic tanks or in open field.</li>
<li>Animal wastes: horse manure, cow-dung, etc. whenever moist and decomposing.</li>
<li>Garbage: whenever moist and exposed. 4. Practically in any moist, rotting organic matter.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="public-health-importance">Public Health importance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#public-health-importance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>â˜‘ the housefly has been known to be the most dangerous contaminant of food, and transmitter of food borne and other diseases.</p>
<p>â˜‘ The housefly is known as a mechanical transmitter of disease agents, which means that it carries through its body parts disease agents (pathogens) from sources of infections to foods, food contact surfaces, to human eyes, and other exposed body parts</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="control-measures">Control Measures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#control-measures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>Better housing and facilities;</li>
<li>Health education;</li>
<li>Delousing with insecticide dusts (10% DDT dust);</li>
<li>Better economy and living standard.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="control-measures">Control Measures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#control-measures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Sanitation Ensuring that neither food nor dirty kitchen utensils are left out over night will help to reduce the number of cockroaches but if they are present in adjoining or near-by houses, good hygiene in itself will not prevent cockroaches from entering houses.</li>
<li>Insecticide application Insecticidal spraying or dusting of selected sites such as cupboards, kitchen furniture and fixtures, stoves, refrigerators and near-by dust bins is recommended.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-rodent">Types of rodent<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-rodent" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Three types of rodent are commonly associated with public health problems.</p>
<ol>
<li>Norway rats (Rattus norvegicus) Also known as the brown rat or sewer rat.</li>
<li>Roof rats (Rattus rattus) also known as the black or grey rat, roof rats are more numerous in rural areas. They live in roofs, and eat mainly grains. They are smaller than Norway rats with longer tails and ears.</li>
<li>Mice â€“ they are smaller in size than rats and generally prefer cereals to eat.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="public-health-importance-of-rodents">Public health importance of rodents<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#public-health-importance-of-rodents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Rodents cause a number of problems:</p>
<ul>
<li>Disease transmission: rats are the natural hosts of fleas that may carry bubonic plague and murine typhus or endemic typhus from an infected rat to a human.</li>
<li>Food damage:</li>
<li>Material damage</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="basic-methods-of-managing-and-controlling-vectors">Basic methods of managing and controlling vectors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#basic-methods-of-managing-and-controlling-vectors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Basic sanitation This approach targets the elimination or reduction of that part of the environment that facilitates breeding and harborage</li>
<li>Physical measures These include methods that stop vectors from getting into close contact with humans, and methods that are used to kill vectors</li>
<li>Use of chemicals Chemical insecticides can be used for the destruction of adults and larvae of insects. Commonly used chemicals are DDT, malathion and pyrethrums.</li>
<li>Biological methods - These include several very advanced methods that prevent the successful reproduction of pest species. such as sterilization</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>of males (tsetse fly, mosquito)</p>
<ul>
<li>Integrated approach Integrated vector management includes a combination of two or more of the above methods. This is often more effective than using a single method of control.</li>
</ul>
<p>Topic name</p>
<p>Hygiene; Personal hygiene</p>
