<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="15-hand-washing-hand-care">15. Hand washing (hand care)-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#15-hand-washing-hand-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>âœ“ Hygienic hand washing involves the mechanical removal of microorganisms from contaminated hand surfaces using soap or detergent.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="hand-washing-technique">Hand washing technique.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hand-washing-technique" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>First wet your hands with clean water and lather with a bar of soap.</li>
<li>Next rub your hands together vigorously and scrub all surfaces up to your wrists.</li>
<li>Clean under your fingernails.</li>
<li>Continue for 15â€“30 seconds. The soap combined with the scrubbing action that helps dislodge and remove germs.</li>
<li>Rinse your hands well with clean running water (pour from a jug or tap).</li>
<li>Dry your hands in the air to avoid recontamination on a dirty towel â€“ do not touch anything until your hands are dry.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="critical-situations-for-hand-wash">Critical situations for hand wash:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#critical-situations-for-hand-wash" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>After using the toilet (or disposing of human or animal faeces)</li>
<li>After changing a babyâ€™s diaper (nappy) and disposing of the faeces.</li>
<li>Immediately after touching raw food when preparing meals (e.g. chicken or other meat).</li>
<li>Before preparing and handling cooked/ready-to-eat food.</li>
<li>Before eating food or feeding children.</li>
<li>After contact with contaminated surfaces (e.g. rubbish bins, cleaning cloths, food-contaminated surfaces).</li>
<li>After handling pets and domestic animals.</li>
<li>After wiping or blowing the nose or sneezing into the hands (respiratory hygiene).</li>
</ul>

<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>After handling soiled tissues (your own or othersâ€™, e.g. children).</p>
<p><strong>Critical situations for hand wash in healthcare:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Before and after contact with an infected wound.</li>
<li>After contact with blood or body fluids (e.g. vomit).</li>
<li>Before and after dressing wounds.</li>
<li>Before giving care to an â€˜at riskâ€™ person (e.g. attending delivery, attending a baby).</li>
<li>After giving care to an infected person.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Community-Led Total Sanitation objective</strong></p>
<p>To define basic CLTS concepts</p>
<p>To enable trainees to understand the guiding principles of CLTS</p>
<p><strong>Definitions</strong></p>
<p><strong>CLTS</strong> refers to Community-Led Total Sanitation. This is an integrated approach to achieving and sustaining open defecation free (ODF) status.</p>
<p>CLTS entails the facilitation of the communityâ€™s analysis of their sanitation profile, their practices of defecation and the consequences, leading to collective action to become ODF</p>
<p><strong>OD</strong> means open defecation â€“ defecating in the open and leaving the stuff exposed.</p>
<p><strong>ODF</strong> means open defecation free, that is, when no faeces are openly exposed to the air.</p>
<p><strong>Natural Leaders (NLs):</strong> are activists and enthusiasts (CLTS champions) who emerge and take the lead during CLTS processes. Men, women, youths and children can all be NLs. Some NLs become community consultants. They trigger and provide encouragement and support to communities other than their own. NLs are active through the processes of construction; innovation; monitoring; developing and implementing community norms and rules;</p>
<p><strong>When CLTS Approach can be used:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>In areas where OD is a common practice.</li>
<li>In communities which have not been previously reached by other hygiene and sanitation interventions.</li>
<li>In communities which have not previously received hardware subsidies for hygiene and sanitation.</li>
<li>Rural communities. However the approach is currently being adjusted to suit urban and peri-urban settings.</li>
</ul>
<p>39</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="advantages-of-clts">advantages of CLTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-clts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>â˜‘ Cost-effective: It is less costly to the promoting organisation since it offers no subsidy.
â˜‘ Delivers quick results: The speed of going total i.e. for an entire community to be ODF in a matter of weeks.
â˜‘ Sustainability: It promotes sustainable sanitation and hygiene practices.
â˜‘ Social solidarity: It enhances social solidarity leading to other actions. The community solidarity and sense of achievement from a successful CLTS process can be an entry point for other livelihood initiatives beyond WASH.
â˜‘ Community ownership: It triggers the communityâ€™s desire for change, propels them into action and encourages innovation, mutual support and appropriate local solutions, thus leading to greater ownership and sustainability.
â˜‘ Community empowerment: CLTS encourages and empowers the community to take responsibility and take its own action.
â˜‘ Emergence of new Natural Leaders (NLs): As the community proceeds towards ODF status, there is spontaneous emergence of new NLs. It also highly encourages new commitment of the existing leaders.
â˜‘ Local actions and innovations: It generates diverse local actions and innovations hence the Community Led Total Sanitation
Participatory and time-bound: It engages men, women, youth and children in a timebound campaign and local action to end OD followed by general cleaning up</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="step-one-pre-triggering">Step One: Pre-Triggering<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#step-one-pre-triggering" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unit-one-principles-of-food-hygiene-and-safety">UNIT ONE: Principles of food hygiene and safety<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-one-principles-of-food-hygiene-and-safety" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Welcome to the last topic of this module where we will get to understand that food is a major determinant of health, nutritional status and productivity of the population. It is, therefore, essential that the food we consume is wholesome and safe. Unsafe food can lead to a large number of food-borne diseases.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-e4bfd5f2.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definitions">Definitions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definitions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>â˜‘ Food Hygiene- refers to Measures and conditions put in place to ensure food safety and quality throughout the entire food chain</li>
<li>â˜‘ Food hygiene is the action taken to ensure that food is handled, stored, prepared and served in such a way, and under such conditions, as to prevent as far as possible - the contamination of food.â€</li>
<li>â˜‘ Food safety is the assurance that food will not cause harm to the consumer when it is prepared and/or eaten according to its intended use</li>
<li>â˜‘ Adulteration is when the normal content of the food has been intentionally changed by adding something to it that is not essential; for example, diluting milk with water and selling it as whole milk. Adulterated food could be unsafe for a number of reasons.</li>
<li>â˜‘ Contamination is the undesired presence of harmful microorganisms or substances in food. Food can be contaminated by unhygienic practices in storage, handling and preparation, and may compromise food safety and palatability.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="objectives-of-food-hygiene">Objectives of Food Hygiene<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives-of-food-hygiene" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Food hygiene is primarily aimed at ensuring the safety, wholesomeness and soundness of food at all stages of production, preparation, marketing and distribution.</li>
</ul>
<p>42</p>
<ul>
<li>In order to achieve the above aim, food quality control services are put in place. Objectives of such services include.</li>
<li>Prevent food losses during harvesting, processing, storage, transportation and handling.</li>
<li>Protect consumers against being offered food that is harmful to health, not fit for human consumption, adulterated or presented in a deceptive manner.</li>
<li>Improve nutrition of the population</li>
<li>Stimulate foreign exchange earning through export of foods that comply with acceptable standards.</li>
<li>Prevent importation of substandard foods</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-hazards-in-food">Types of Hazards in food<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-hazards-in-food" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Hazard is the relative probability that harm or injury will result when substance is not used in a prescribed manner and quantity.</p>
<p>Hazards can be physical, chemical and biological causing harmful / adverse effects on the health of consumers.</p>
<ol>
<li>Physical hazard is any physical material not normally found in food, which causes illness or injury and includes wood, stones, parts of pests, hair etc</li>
<li>Chemical hazards are chemicals or deleterious substances which may be intentionally or un-intentionally added to foods. This category of hazards includes pesticides, chemical residues, toxic metals, polychlorinated biphenyls, preservatives, food colours and other additives</li>
<li>Biological hazards are living organisms and include microbiological organisms. Those micro-organisms which are associated with food and cause diseases are termed food-borne pathogens.</li>
</ol>
<p>There are two types of food-borne diseases from microbial pathogensâ€”infections and poisoning.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sources-of-food-contamination">Sources of Food Contamination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources-of-food-contamination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These may be classified under the following:</p>
<ol>
<li>Food handlers</li>
<li>Equipment</li>
</ol>

<ol start="3">
<li>Chemicals</li>
<li>Pests/parasites</li>
<li>Water</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="routes-of-microbial-contamination-of-food">Routes of microbial contamination of food<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#routes-of-microbial-contamination-of-food" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Bacteria are a major source of microbial contamination of food, i.e. the undesired presence in food of harmful microorganisms or the harmful substances they produce.</li>
<li>Viruses, parasites and fungi are also able to contaminate food and cause foodborne illnesses in humans.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="air-and-dust">Air and dust<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#air-and-dust" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Microorganisms are found everywhere in our environment.</li>
<li>Many types can be found in air and dust, and can contaminate food at any time during food preparation or when food is left uncovered.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="soil-water-and-plants">Soil, water and plants<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#soil-water-and-plants" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Many microorganisms present in soil and water can contaminate foods.</li>
<li>Microorganisms also grow on plants and can contaminate food if care is not taken to remove them by washing or inactivate them by cooking.</li>
<li>Soil is a particularly rich source of <em>Clostridium</em> bacteria. Water may be contaminated by faeces. Plants may also be contaminated by faeces if untreated sewage has been used as a fertiliser.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="gastrointestinal-tract">Gastrointestinal tract<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gastrointestinal-tract" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The intestines of all humans and animals are full of microorganisms, some of which are beneficial but others are pathogenic.</li>
<li>Bacterial pathogens such as <em>Salmonella</em>, <em>Campylobacter</em> and <em>Escherichia coli</em> (strain O157:H7) are common examples.</li>
<li>Contamination of foods by faecal material is the major cause of food poisoning events.</li>
<li>This includes indirect contamination, for example from peopleâ€™s hands if they prepare food without washing their hands after visiting the latrine/toilet.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="animals">Animals<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#animals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Many foodborne microorganisms are present in healthy animals raised for food, usually in their intestines, hides, feathers, etc. Meat and poultry carcasses can be contaminated during slaughter by contact with small amounts of intestinal contents.</li>
<li>Animal hides are a primary source of <em>E.coli</em> O157:H7 and <em>Salmonella</em> species, both of which cause sickness and diarrhoea.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="animal-feeds">Animal feeds<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#animal-feeds" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Animal feeds are a source of microorganisms, especially <em>Salmonella</em>, which can contaminate poultry and other farm animals.</li>
<li>The organisms in dry animal feed spread throughout the local environment and may get on to animal hides, hair and feathers, as well as on people who handle the feeds.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="food-handlers">Food handlers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#food-handlers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The term <strong>food handler</strong> can be applied to anyone who touches or handles food, and this</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>includes people who process, transport, prepare, cook and serve food.</p>
<p>â˜‘ The presence of microorganisms on the hands and outer garments of food handlers reflects the standard of hygiene in the environment and the individuals' personal hygiene (as you learned in earlier study sessions).
â˜‘ The microorganisms transmitted to foods by food handlers may come from the hides of animals, soil, water, dust, gastrointestinal tracts and other environmental sources.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="food-utensils">Food utensils<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#food-utensils" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>â˜‘ These are cutting boards, knives, spoons, bowls and other equipment used in food preparation, which may become contaminated during food processing and preparation. For example, in families where there is no access to running water, the food utensils may not be properly cleaned, stored and handled, and may become a major route of food contamination.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cross-contamination">Cross-contamination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cross-contamination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>â˜‘ Cross-contamination of food is the transfer of harmful microorganisms between food items and food contact surfaces.
â˜‘ Prepared food, utensils and surfaces may become contaminated by raw food products and microorganisms.
â˜‘ These can be transferred from one food to another by using the same knife, cutting board or other utensil without washing it between uses.
â˜‘ A food that is fully cooked can become re-contaminated if it touches raw foods or contaminated surfaces or utensils that contain pathogens.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unsafe-temperature">Unsafe temperature<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unsafe-temperature" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>â˜‘ An unsafe temperature for food storage is a major factor in food contamination.
â˜‘ Many microorganisms need to multiply to a very large number before enough are present in food to cause disease in someone who eats it. However, if bacteria can have warm, moist conditions and an ample supply of nutrients, one bacterium can reproduce by dividing (on average) every half an hour and can produce 17 million bacteria in 12 hours! So, if you leave lightly contaminated food out overnight, it will be highly contaminated and infectious by the next day.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="poor-personal-hygiene">Poor personal hygiene<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#poor-personal-hygiene" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>â˜‘ Poor personal hygiene of food handlers is another major factor in food contamination.
â˜‘ The most important contaminants of food are the microorganisms excreted with faeces from the intestinal tract of humans.
â˜‘ These pathogens are transferred to the food from faecal matter present on the hands.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="food-spoilage">Food Spoilage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#food-spoilage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="food-spoilage-agents">Food Spoilage agents<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#food-spoilage-agents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) Microorganisms
i. Bacteria- main food spoilage agents
ii. Viruses
iii. Fungi- Yeasts and moulds
b) Enzymes
c) Chemical Reactions
d) Physical Reactions
e) Insects, rodents, and birds</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-food-spoilage">Types of food spoilage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-food-spoilage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Definition:</strong> Spoiled food may be defined as food that has been damaged or injured so as to make it undesirable for human use.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-microbial-spoilage">1) Microbial Spoilage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-microbial-spoilage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Microbial spoilage arises from the normal function of these organisms in the total ecology of all living organisms. In their normal metabolic processes, microorganisms destroy plant and animal organic matter by converting it into inorganic compounds. These primary activities of Microorganisms on foods bring about the phenomenon called spoilage.</p>
<p>Change in taste, smell, colour, texture and appearance are the main features of microbial spoilage.</p>
<p>The primary causative agents of microbial spoilage are the bacteria, yeasts and moulds.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="signs-of-microbial-food-spoilage">Signs of Microbial Food Spoilage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-of-microbial-food-spoilage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>â˜‘ Odour: â€œoff odoursâ€ are smells (sometimes like rotten eggs) that are produced when bacteria break down the protein in foods, (usually fatty foods). This process is called <em>putrefaction</em>.</li>
<li>â˜‘ Sliminess: Food becomes slimy as the bacterial population grows. The sliminess is due to long chains of bacteria such as streptococcus.</li>
<li>â˜‘ Discoloration: Foods may be discoloured by microbial growth. The coloration is due to coloured spores that give the food a distinctive colour, e.g. black pin mould on bread, or blue and green mould on citrus fruit and cheese.</li>
<li>â˜‘ Souring: Foods go sour when certain bacteria produce acids. A common example is when milk sours from the production of lactic acid.</li>
<li>â˜‘ Gas production: Bacteria and yeasts often produce gaseous by-products that can affect food e.g. meat becoming spongy, swelling of canned food or a popping sound on open</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Enzymic and Chemical Spoilage</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Also referred to as autolysis. Autolysis is self-digestion emanating from factors within the food tissues themselves. These factors are mainly enzymes and chemical compounds. Examples of such spoilage are:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Enzymatic browning - it is initiated by the enzyme polyphenol oxidase (polyphenolase). The action of this enzyme results in slightly brown discoloration accompanied by undesirable changes in flavor and texture in fruits and vegetables e.g. apples, potatoes, avocados, beetroot etc.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In order for the browning to occur three components must be present - the enzyme, the substrate (phenolic compounds) and oxygen</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Non-enzymatic browning â€“ Brought about by chemicals. It is found in many foods other than fruits, and results from a reaction between reducing sugars and compounds containing amino groups, which produce a dark-brown substance called malanoidines.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An example of non-enzymic browning is the browning of heated milk.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>Insects, rodents and birds</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Insects and rodents may infect food by infecting organisms with their saliva or deposit them with their excreta.</li>
<li>They also greatly destroy the quality of grains e.g. weevils burrowing in maize grains</li>
<li>Rodents lower the nutritive value of maize by eating the germ.</li>
<li>Birds can significantly lower the amount of harvest of some cereals by feeding on them while still in the field.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>Physical Injuries</li>
</ol>
<p>These can be in form of:</p>
<ul>
<li>Crushing/breaking due to excessive mechanical forces</li>
<li>Bruises arising from poor handling methods</li>
<li>Injuries from preservation methods e.g. "freezer burn" and "cold shortening" resulting from freezing.</li>
</ul>
<p>Factors affecting the rate of food spoilage</p>
<ul>
<li>The nature of the food itself - in providing nutrients for microbial growth</li>
<li>The initial microbial load in food</li>
<li>Moisture content of food</li>
<li>PH of the food</li>
<li>Temperature of air in storage environment.</li>
<li>Composition of air in storage environment.</li>
<li>Humidity of the storage environment.</li>
<li>Exposure to sunlight</li>
</ul>
<p>47</p>
<p>The criteria for assurance in foods suitable for consumption are: â€¢</p>
<ul>
<li>The desired stage of development or maturity of the food.</li>
<li>Freedom from pollution at any stage in the production and subsequent handling of the food.</li>
<li>Freedom from objectionable, chemical and physical changes resulting from action of food enzymes; activity of microbes, insects, rodents, invasion of parasites; and damage from pressure, freezing, heating, drying, and the like.</li>
<li>Freedom from micro-organisms and parasites causing food borne illnesses</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="food-borne-diseases">Food Borne Diseases<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#food-borne-diseases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Food borne diseases is defined as a disease caused by agents that enter the body through the ingestion of contaminated food. These agents may be infectious agents or toxic substances.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification-of-food-borne-diseases">Classification of Food borne diseases<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-food-borne-diseases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Food borne infections:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>They are diseases whose etiologic agents are viable pathogenic organisms ingested with foods and that can establish infection.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Food poisonings/ intoxications:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Diseases arising from the ingestion of toxins released by microorganisms, intoxications from poisonous plants or toxic animal tissues, or due to consumption of food contaminated by chemical poisons.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sources-of-food-poisoning">Sources of food poisoning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources-of-food-poisoning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) Chemicals - e.g. cadmium from utensils, sodium fluoride that may be accidentally added to food.
b) Plants - poisoning may result from consumption of plants or their products e.g. young fava beans, poisonous mushrooms etc.
c) Animals - e.g. consumption of ocean mussels and crabs during certain seasons of the year when they may contain a poisonous alkali.
d) Microorganisms and their toxins - these are by far the most common sources of foodborne diseases and the learner is therefore most likely to encounter these kind of outbreaks in his or her practice. It is therefore necessary to deal with this type of illnesses in greater detail.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="high-risk-foods">High-risk foods<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#high-risk-foods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>They are ready to eat foods that under unfavorable conditions support the multiplication of harmful bacteria and intended for consumption without treatment which would destroy such organisms.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>High risk foods are most likely to be involved in cases of food poisoning.</p>
<p>They are usually high in protein and moisture, requiring strict temperature control and protection from contamination</p>
<p>They include:</p>
<ul>
<li>â˜‘ All cooked meat and poultry</li>
<li>â˜‘ Milk cream, custards, dairy products and ice cream</li>
<li>â˜‘ Cooked eggs, especially those made with raw eggs and not thoroughly cooked, for example mayonnaise</li>
<li>â˜‘ Sea food for example cooked prawns</li>
<li>â˜‘ Cooked rice (not high in protein)</li>
</ul>
<p>Low-risk foods</p>
<p>They are rarely implicated in food poisoning and may be stored, suitably packaged, at ambient temperatures.</p>
<p>They do not support multiplication of food poisoning bacteria.</p>
<p>Some examples include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Preserved food such as jam;</li>
<li>Dried foods or food with little moisture, such as flour, rice bread or biscuits. But once liquid has been added to powered food, such as milk, the food becomes high risk;</li>
<li>Acid foods such as vinegar or products stored in vinegar;</li>
<li>Fermented products;</li>
<li>Foods with high fat/sugar content, such as chocolate; and</li>
<li>Canned foods, whilst unopened.</li>
</ul>
<p>Common Food Poisoning Illnesses</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>CLOSTRIDIUM PERFRINGENS</th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Foods involved</td><td>Contaminated poultry meat and meat products, especially stews, gravies and pies.</td></tr><tr><td>Main Symptoms</td><td>Abdominal pain, diarrhoea and nausea.</td></tr><tr><td>Onset of Illness</td><td>8 to 22 hours, (usually 10 to 12 hours).</td></tr><tr><td>Source</td><td>This organism is found in the waste of animals and man, and often in raw meat and in soil.</td></tr></tbody></table>

Meat, eggs and fish products.</td></tr><tr><td>Main Symptoms</td><td>Abdominal pain, severe vomiting, diarrhea, abdominal cramps, and sometimes collapse.</td></tr><tr><td>Onset of Illness</td><td>1 to 6 hours (usually 2 to 4 hours).</td></tr><tr><td>Source</td><td>Staphylococcal bacteria may come from infected sores, nasal secretions and skin (perspiration and hair).</td></tr><tr><td>The toxin that causes illness can survive ordinary cooking.</td><td></td></tr><tr><td><strong>CAMPYLOBACTER</strong></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Foods involved</td><td>Contaminated meat and meat products, especially poultry.</td></tr><tr><td>Contaminated water, and raw milk.</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Main Symptoms</td><td>Diarrhoea, abdominal pain, fever, nausea, and vomiting.</td></tr><tr><td>Onset of Illness</td><td>1 to 10 days (usually 3 to 5 days).</td></tr></tbody></table>

<li>Too long between preparation and consumption.</li>

<ol start="5">
<li>Cross-contamination from raw to high risk/ready to eat foods.</li>
<li>Infected food handlers.</li>
<li>Inadequate hot holding temperatures.</li>
<li>Inadequate hand washing.</li>
<li>Contaminated raw foods and ingredients.</li>
<li>Improper cleaning of equipment and utensils.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-of-food-poisoning">PREVENTION OF FOOD POISONING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-of-food-poisoning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In most cases of food poisoning a chain of events takes place, and if we are to reduce the incidence of illness, this chain must be broken.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-food-poisoning-chain">THE FOOD POISONING CHAIN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-food-poisoning-chain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-cd4d50ae.jpeg" alt="img-5.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="there-are-three-main-ways-of-breaking-the-food-poisoning-chain">There are three main ways of breaking the food poisoning chain -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#there-are-three-main-ways-of-breaking-the-food-poisoning-chain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Protecting food from contamination.</li>
<li>Preventing any bacteria present in the food from multiplying.</li>
<li>Destroying those bacteria that are present in the food.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="protecting-food-from-contamination-by">Protecting food from contamination by -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#protecting-food-from-contamination-by" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Inspecting all food and washing fruit and vegetables before preparation.</li>
<li>Separating raw and high risk/ready to eat foods at all stages of preparation, storage, display and distribution.</li>
</ul>
<p>The same equipment, utensils and working surfaces must not be used to handle raw and high risk/ready to eat foods.</p>
<ul>
<li>Only handling food when unavoidable.
Gloves, tongs and other utensils, plates and trays should be used in preference to hands, (but must be washed or changed frequently).</li>
<li>Keeping food covered as much as possible.</li>
<li>Preventing insects, animals and birds from entering food rooms.</li>
<li>Not using unsuitable, defective, or dirty equipment.</li>
<li>Using good personal hygiene practices - always.</li>
<li>Not coughing or sneezing over or around food.</li>
<li>Not handling the food contact surfaces of crockery, cutlery or utensils.</li>
<li>All food handlers wearing suitable protective clothing.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Using the correct cleaning procedures.</li>
<li>Promptly removing unfit or waste food and refuse from food areas.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preventing-any-bacteria-within-food-from-multiplying-by">Preventing any bacteria within food from multiplying by -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preventing-any-bacteria-within-food-from-multiplying-by" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Keeping high risk foods at temperatures that inhibit the growth of bacteria (i.e. out of the danger zone). Food should be kept below 4Â°C in a refrigerated unit or above 70Â°C in a suitable warming unit.</li>
<li>Ensuring that during preparation, food is in the danger zone for as short a time as possible. High risk foods must not be left sitting out at room temperature.</li>
<li>Using suitable preservatives such as salt and sugar.</li>
<li>Using various packing methods like gas flushing or vacuum packing.</li>
<li>Not allowing dried foods to absorb moisture.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="destroying-those-bacteria-within-food-by">Destroying those bacteria within food by -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#destroying-those-bacteria-within-food-by" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Adequately cooking food, ensuring that a minimum internal cooking temperature of 80Â°C is reached.</li>
<li>Heat processing such as pasteurization, sterilization or canning.</li>
</ul>
<p>A combination of a suitable temperature and sufficient time is always required to destroy bacteria. The time and temperature required will depend on the particular organism, (e.g. spores of <em>Clostridium perfringens</em> are much more heat resistant than <em>Salmonella</em> bacteria).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives-of-investigating-an-outbreak-of-a-food-borne-disease">objectives of investigating an outbreak of a food-borne disease<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives-of-investigating-an-outbreak-of-a-food-borne-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>â˜‘ Identify the causative agent responsible for the outbreak</li>
<li>â˜‘ Identify the food items, handlers, etc. responsible for the outbreak</li>
<li>â˜‘ Identify and trace the location of the source of the outbreak</li>
<li>â˜‘ Determine the conditions and mechanisms that led to the contamination of the food item identified, e.g. perform sanitary survey</li>
<li>â˜‘ Limit the impacts and arrest the progression of the outbreak</li>
<li>â˜‘ Be able to use information obtained from the current outbreak for the prevention of subsequent outbreaks</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="steps-in-the-investigation-of-food-borne-disease-outbreak-investigation">steps in the investigation of food-borne disease outbreak investigation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#steps-in-the-investigation-of-food-borne-disease-outbreak-investigation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Verify the existence of an outbreak. Compare the current number of cases with the past
Note: -consider seasonal variations</li>
<li>Verify the diagnosis. Review clinical and laboratory findings</li>
<li>Describe the outbreak with respect to time, place and person</li>
<li>Prepare an epidemic curve</li>
<li>Calculate food-specific attack rates</li>
<li>Formulate and test hypotheses (by consulting with higher level health professionals). 7. Search for additional cases</li>
<li>Analyse the data</li>
</ol>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="8">
<li>Make a decision on the hypotheses tested (by consulting with higher level health professionals).</li>
<li>Intervene and follow-up</li>
<li>Report the investigation</li>
<li>Inform the public on the control and prevention of the outbreak</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="five-keys-to-safe-food">FIVE KEYS TO SAFE FOOD<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#five-keys-to-safe-food" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="keep-clean">Keep clean<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#keep-clean" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Wash your hands before handling food and often during food preparation.</li>
<li>Wash, and sanitize all surfaces and equipment used for food preparation.</li>
<li>â˜‘ Utensils especially those from which you eat, drink or in which you cook should not come in touch with raw meat/poultry/eggs.</li>
<li>Protect kitchen areas and food from insects, pests and other animals.</li>
<li>â˜‘ Keep food covered, in closed containers and wherever needed, refrigerated.</li>
<li>â˜‘ Keep food preparation area clean and in good condition (repair cracks, fill holes, do not allow small spaces between fixtures that do not allow cleaning and where dirt and food can accumulate).</li>
<li>â˜‘ Do not neglect the rubbish area. Keep it clean and tidy and remove rubbish daily. Clean and dry all equipment (including the cleaning equipment) as germs can grow fast in damp places.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="separate-raw-and-cooked">Separate raw and cooked<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#separate-raw-and-cooked" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>â˜‘ Separate raw meat, poultry and seafood from other foods at all stages from cleaning, storing, preparation, and cooking.</li>
<li>â˜‘ Use separate equipment, utensils (including washcloth) for handling raw foods meats, poultry and seafood.</li>
<li>â˜‘ Do not let juices or liquids from raw meats, poultry and seafood to spill or seep onto other surfaces or come into contact with cooked or other raw foods.</li>
<li>â˜‘ Store foods in covered containers to avoid cross-contamination between raw and prepared foods.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="cook-thoroughly">Cook thoroughly<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cook-thoroughly" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>â˜‘ Ensure food is thoroughly cooked through, especially meat, poultry, eggs and seafood.</li>
<li>â˜‘ Juices from meats, seafood and poultry should not be pink, and should be clear.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="store-food-at-safe-temperatures">Store food at safe temperatures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#store-food-at-safe-temperatures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>â˜‘ Do not leave cooked food at room temperatures for more than 2 hours.</li>
<li>â˜‘ Refrigerate all cooked and perishable foods promptly</li>
<li>â˜‘ Keep cooked food very hot (above 60Â°C) prior to serving</li>
<li>â˜‘ Do not store food too long (more than 3 days) in the refrigerator</li>
<li>â˜‘ Do not reheat refrigerator food more than once.</li>
<li>â˜‘ Do not refreeze frozen food after thawing or cooking</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="use-safe-water-and-raw-materials">Use safe water and raw materials.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#use-safe-water-and-raw-materials" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>â˜‘ Use safe water or treat it (by boiling, chlorination, and filtration) to make it safe for cooking, washing hands or utensils, and making drinks or ice.</li>
<li>â˜‘ Select fresh and wholesome foods (not damaged or rotting) from clean stores / places</li>
<li>â˜‘ Wash fruits and vegetables, especially if eaten raw</li>
<li>â˜‘ Cut away damaged or bruised parts of fruits and vegetables, since bacteria can thrive in these places.</li>
</ul>

<p>â˜‘ Do not use food beyond their expiry date.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="common-methods-of-food-preservation">COMMON METHODS OF FOOD PRESERVATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-methods-of-food-preservation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Principles of Food Preservation include the following:</p>
<p>i) Prevention or delay of microbial decomposition.</p>
<ul>
<li>â˜‘ By keeping microbes out (asepsis).</li>
<li>â˜‘ By removal of microbes (e.g. filtration).</li>
<li>â˜‘ By reducing the rate of microbial growth (e.g. by low temperature, drying, anaerobic conditions and chemical inhibitors).</li>
<li>â˜‘ By killing microbes (e.g. by heat or radiation).</li>
</ul>
<p>ii) Prevention or delay of self-decomposition of food</p>
<ul>
<li>â˜‘ By inactivation of food enzymes (e.g. blanching).</li>
<li>â˜‘ By prevention of chemical reactions (e.g. by using antioxidants).</li>
</ul>

        // Theme toggle functionality
        const themeToggle = document.getElementById('theme-toggle');
        const html = document.documentElement;
        
        themeToggle.addEventListener('click', () => {
            const currentTheme = html.getAttribute('data-theme');
            const newTheme = currentTheme === 'light' ? 'dark' : 'light';
            
            html.setAttribute('data-theme', newTheme);
            localStorage.setItem('theme', newTheme);
        });
        
        // Load saved theme
        const savedTheme = localStorage.getItem('theme') || 'light';
        html.setAttribute('data-theme', savedTheme);
    </script>
